                  </form>, (T,) or <foreign lang="ar">استظلّ بِالِظِّلِّ</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a man, T) <hi rend="ital">sheltered,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">protected, himself by means of the shade:</hi> (T, TA:) or the latter means <hi rend="ital">he inclined to the shade and sat in it.</hi> (M, K.) And <foreign lang="ar">استظلّ مِنَ الشَّىْءِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بِهِ</foreign> means   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27590-1" target="تَظَلَّلَ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27589-3"/></foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">he shaded himself</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">تظلّل</foreign> being quasi-pass. of <foreign lang="ar">ظَلَّلَهُ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">from the thing</hi> and <hi rend="ital">by means of it</hi>]. (M, K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">استظلّ بِهِ مِنَ الشَّمْسِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He shaded himself with it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by means of it, from the sun</hi>]. (T.) And <foreign lang="ar">استظلّ بِالشَّجَرَةِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He shaded and sheltered himself by means of the tree.</hi> (Ibn-'Abbád, S, O.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">استظلّ الدَّمُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The blood was in the</hi>

                  <foreign lang="ar">الجَوْفِ</foreign> is put for <foreign lang="ar">فِى الجَوْفِ</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">استظلّت العَيْنُ</foreign>, <pb n="1915"/> (T, Ibn-'Abbád, O,) or <foreign lang="ar">العُيُونُ</foreign>, (K,) <hi rend="ital">The eye,</hi> (T, Ibn-'Abbád, O,) meaning that of a she-camel, (Ibn-'Abbád, O,) or <hi rend="ital">the eyes,</hi> (K,) <hi rend="ital">sank,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became depressed, in the head.</hi> (T, Ibn-'Abbád, O, K.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">استظلّ الكَرْمُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The grape-vine became luxuriant,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abundant and dense, in its branches whereon were the bunches.</hi> (M, K.)    </entryFree>26:T4eef,<entryFree id="n27591" key="ظِلٌّ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ظِلٌّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> properly signifies <hi rend="ital">Shade;</hi> i. e. the <hi rend="ital">light of the sun without the rays:</hi> when there is no light, it is <foreign lang="ar">ظُلْمَةٌ</foreign>, not <foreign lang="ar">ظِلٌّ</foreign>: (S, O:) <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ضِحٌّ</foreign>: (M, K:) or <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَىْءٌ</foreign>: (K:) so some say: (M:) or so the [common] people say: (IKt, Msb:) or the former is [<hi rend="ital">shade</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in the morning;</hi> and the latter is in the evening: (M, K:) or, accord. to IKt, the former is <hi rend="ital">in the morning and in the evening;</hi> but the latter is only after the declining of the sun from the meridian: ISk says that the former is <hi rend="ital">from the rising of the sun to its declining;</hi> and the latter, from the declining to the setting: Th says that the <foreign lang="ar">ظِلّ</foreign> of a tree &amp;c. is <hi rend="ital">in the morning;</hi> and the <foreign lang="ar">فَىْء</foreign>, in the evening: (Msb:) Ru-beh says, (M, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">any place,</hi> (M,) or <hi rend="ital">any thing,</hi> (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">upon which the sun has been and which it has quitted</hi> is termed <foreign lang="ar">ظِلٌّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">فَىْءٌ</foreign>; (M, Msb;) but <hi rend="ital">a thing</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">place</hi>] <hi rend="ital">upon which the sun has not been</hi> is termed <foreign lang="ar">ظِلٌّ</foreign> [only]; and hence it is said that the sun annuls, or supersedes, the <foreign lang="ar">ظِلّ</foreign>, and the <foreign lang="ar">فَىْء</foreign> annuls, or supersedes, the sun: (Msb:) AHeyth says, the <foreign lang="ar">ظِلّ</foreign> is <hi rend="ital">anything upon which the sun has not come;</hi> and the term <foreign lang="ar">فَىْء</foreign> is applied only after the declining of the sun; the <foreign lang="ar">فَىْء</foreign> being eastwards and the <foreign lang="ar">ظِلّ</foreign> being westwards; and the <foreign lang="ar">ظِلّ</foreign> being termed <foreign lang="ar">ظِلّ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">from the beginning of the day to the declining of the sun;</hi> after which it is termed <foreign lang="ar">فَىْء</foreign> until the night: (T, TA:) one says the <foreign lang="ar">ظِلّ</foreign> of Paradise, but not its <foreign lang="ar">فَىْء</foreign>, because the sun will never replace its <foreign lang="ar">ظِلّ</foreign>; but En-Nábighah El-Jaadee has assigned to Paradise <foreign lang="ar">فَىْء</foreign> having <foreign lang="ar">ظِلَال</foreign>: (M, TA:) in a verse of Aboo-Sakhr ElHudhalee, <foreign lang="ar">ظِلٌّ</foreign> is made fem. as meaning <foreign lang="ar">مَنِيَّة</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">death</hi>]: (Ham p. 161:) the pl. [of mult.] is <foreign lang="ar">ظِلَالٌ</foreign> (S, M, O, K) and <foreign lang="ar">ظُلُولٌ</foreign> and [of pauc.] <foreign lang="ar">أَظْلَالٌ</foreign>. (M, O, K.) The saying of a rájiz, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">كَأَنَّمَا وَجْهُكَ ظِلٌّ مِنْ حَجَرْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">As though thy face were a shade of a stone</hi>] is said to mean hardness of face, and shamelessness: or the being black in the face: (T, TA:) for the Arabs say that there is nothing more dense in shade than a stone. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ ضَحَا ظِلُّهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">His shade,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">shadow, has become sun</hi>] is said of the dead. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ بِنَا كَأَنَّهُ ظِلُّ ذِئْبٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He passed by us as though he were the shadow of a wolf</hi>] means swiftly, as does a wolf. (M.) <foreign lang="ar">اِنْتَعَلَتْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ظِلَالَهَا</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">They made their shadows to be as though they were sandals to them</hi>] is said of camels or other beasts when it is midday in summer and they have no shadow [but such as is beneath them]: a rájiz says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ وَرَدَتْ تَمْشِى عَلَى ظِلَالِهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَذَابَتِ الشَّمْسُ عَلَى قِلَالِهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">They came to the water walking upon their shadows, and the sun was intensely hot upon the tops of their heads and humps</hi>]. (T.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ يَتْبَعُ ظِلَّ نَفْسِهِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He follows the shadow of himself;</hi> i. e. a thing that he will not overtake; for], as a poet says, the shadow that goes with thee thou wilt not overtake by following: and <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ يُبَارِى ظِلَّ نَفْسِهِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He strives to outstrip the shadow of himself</hi>], meaning that he walks with a proud and self-conceited gait: so in the A. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">اِنْتَقَلْتُ عَنْ ظِلِّى</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">I left my state,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">condition.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">تَرَكَ الظَّبْىُ ظِلَّهُ</foreign>: so in the T and S and O: (TA:) but [said to be] correctly, <foreign lang="ar">أَتْرُكُهُ تَرْكَ الظَّبْىِ ظِلَّهُ</foreign>, (K,) or <foreign lang="ar">لَأَتْرُكَنَّهُ</foreign>, (M, TA,) i. e. [<hi rend="ital">I will forsake him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I will assuredly forsake him, as the gazelle forsakes</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the place of its shade:</hi> (O, TA:) [each, however, is app. right; and the former is the more agreeable with the following explanations:] a prov., (M,) applied to the man who is wont to take fright and flee; for the gazelle, when it takes fright and flees from a thing, never returns to it: (S, O, K:) by the <foreign lang="ar">ظِلّ</foreign> is here meant the covert in which it shades and shelters itself in the vehemence of the heat; then the hunter comes to it and rouses it, and it will not return thither; and one says, <foreign lang="ar">تَرَكَ الظَّبْىُ ظِلَّهُ</foreign>, meaning the place of its shade: it is applied to him who takes fright and flees from a thing, and forsakes it so as not to return to it; and to the case of a man's forsaking his companion. (Meyd.) [<foreign lang="ar">ثَقِيلُ الظِّلِّ</foreign> as applied to a man, see expl. in art. <foreign lang="ar">ثقل</foreign>: see also Har p. 250, where it is indicated that it may be rendered One <hi rend="ital">whose shadow,</hi> even, <hi rend="ital">is oppressive,</hi> and therefore much more so is his person.] In the phrase <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا ٱلظِّلُّ وَلَا ٱلْحَرُورُ</foreign>, (M, K) in the Kur [xxxv. 20], Th says, accord. to some, (M,) <foreign lang="ar">الظِّلُّ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">Paradise;</hi> (M, K;) and <foreign lang="ar">الحَرُورُ</foreign>, the fire [of Hell]: but he adds, I say that <foreign lang="ar">الظِّلُّ</foreign> is the <foreign lang="ar">ظِلّ</foreign> itself [i. e. <hi rend="ital">shade</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">الحَرُورُ</foreign> is the <foreign lang="ar">حَرّ</foreign> itself [i. e. heat]: (M: [see also <foreign lang="ar">حَرُورٌ</foreign>:]) and Er-Rághib says that <foreign lang="ar">ظِلٌّ</foreign> is sometimes assigned to anything; whether it be approved, as in the phrase above mentioned; or disapproved, as in <foreign lang="ar">وَظِلٍّ مِنْ يَحْمُومٍ</foreign> in the Kur [lvi. 42, meaning <hi rend="ital">And shade of smoke,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">black smoke</hi>]. (TA.)
